<p><i><b>Left 4 Dead 2</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_gameplay" title="Cooperative gameplay">cooperative</a> <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> developed and published by <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve Corporation</a>. The sequel to <a href="/wiki/Turtle_Rock_Studios" title="Turtle Rock Studios">Turtle Rock Studios</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead" title="Left 4 Dead">Left 4 Dead</a></i>, the game released for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> in November 2009, and for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OS_X" title="OS X">OS X</a> in October 2010, and for <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> in July 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steam_News_4436_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steam_News_4436-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Left_4_Dead_Blog_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Left_4_Dead_Blog-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> builds upon cooperatively focused gameplay and Valve's proprietary <a href="/wiki/Source_(game_engine)" title="Source (game engine)">Source engine</a>, the same game engine used in the original <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. Set during the aftermath of an apocalyptic pandemic, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> focuses on four new Survivors, fighting against hordes of zombies, known as the Infected, who develop severe psychosis and act extremely aggressive. The Survivors must fight their way through five campaigns, interspersed with <a href="/wiki/Safe_house" title="Safe house">safe houses</a> that act as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continue_point" title="Continue point">checkpoints</a>, with the goal of escape at each campaign's finale. The gameplay is <a href="/wiki/Procedural_generation" title="Procedural generation">procedurally altered</a> by the "<a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">AI</a> Director 2.0", which monitors the players' performance and adjusts the <a href="/wiki/Scenario" title="Scenario">scenario</a> to provide a dynamic challenge. Other new features include new types of special infected and an arsenal of <a href="/wiki/Melee_weapon" title="Melee weapon">melee weapons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game made its world premiere at <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3 2009</a> with a trailer during the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> press event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e3preview_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-e3preview-4">[4]</a></sup> Prior to release, it received a combination of positive and negative critical and community reactions. It attracted an unusually high volume of pre-release controversy about the game's graphic content. In response, alterations were made to the cover art<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coverart_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-coverart-5">[5]</a></sup> and both Australia and Germany refused to rate the unmodified edition at the time of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ban_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-ban-6">[6]</a></sup> After release however, the game was met with positive reviews by critics.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like its predecessor, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> is a first-person shooter with a heavy emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_gameplay" title="Cooperative gameplay">cooperative gameplay</a>. The game presents five new campaigns, each composed of three to five smaller levels. As in the first game, each campaign is presented in menus and loading screens as a film starring the four Survivors; and features, upon completing a campaign, a faux credits screen which acts as the final scoreboard for the players and recaps certain performance statistics for the group. In every campaign, most levels involve the Survivors attempting to reach a safe zone and close the door once they are all safely inside. However, the final level in each campaign requires the Survivors to call for rescue and either survive a prolonged onslaught until rescue arrives, pass through an especially challenging gauntlet of Infected to reach an escape vehicle, or (in <i><a href="#Story">Dead Center</a></i> and <i><a href="#DLC_campaigns">The Passing</a></i>) collect and utilize fuel cans to enable their escape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dc_04_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-dc_04-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-passing_03_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-passing_03-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each Survivor can carry one of each five categories of equipment. The main weapons are broken down into four tiers based on their availability and attributes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Tier one weapons (such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">SMG</a></i> and <i>Chrome Shotgun</i>) have a low ratio of damage for time, and serve as basic offensive weapons. Tier two weapons (such as the <i>Assault Rifle</i> and <i>Combat Shotgun</i>) carry a higher amount of damage per time unit and often appear in later maps of each chapter. The two tier three weapons (<i>Grenade Launcher</i> and <i>M60</i>) differ from one and two in the fact that they cannot refill their ammunition from ammunition dumps and generally there is only one or two (at most) of each per map. They carry a high damage ratio at the cost of limited ammo. Tier four weapons are all mounted weapon systems and carry unlimited ammunition. The mounted weapons carry the highest damage ratio, but at the cost of overheating after a period of non-stop use. The mounted weapons are in set positions in maps and have a fixed arc of fire. They cannot be given ammunition pack upgrades to the bullets or utilize the laser sights attachment. Either a melee weapon or pistols are used as secondary weapons. Although melee weapons cause extra damage to Infected when struck, the Survivors can use any other weapon or item for weaker melee attacks that can push the Infected back. Players also carry a flashlight with infinite battery life, the use of which enables players to see in the dark (with the downside of the player gaining the attention of the Infected much faster). They may also carry a single <a href="/wiki/First_aid_kit" title="First aid kit">first aid kit</a>, special ammo pack, or a <a href="/wiki/Defibrillation" title="Defibrillation">defibrillator</a>; in addition to either pain pills or an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adrenaline" title="Adrenaline">adrenaline</a> shot. They may also carry a single throwable weapon—<a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktails</a> to set an area on fire; <a href="/wiki/Pipe_bomb" title="Pipe bomb">pipe bombs</a> to attract any nearby Infected to the flashing light and sound it makes until it explodes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and Boomer <a href="/wiki/Bile" title="Bile">bile</a>, which attracts Common Infected to whatever it hits (e.g. fires, Special Infected, each other).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>To enable situational awareness of other Survivors, players are shown the health and status of their fellow survivors. If a player does not have direct sight of another Survivor (e.g. a wall is blocking their view of the others), they will be shown the Survivor's highlighted silhouette. The Survivors are also susceptible to <a href="/wiki/Friendly_fire" title="Friendly fire">friendly fire</a>, forcing players to exercise caution when shooting or swinging their weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> As Survivors take damage, they move more slowly; if a Survivor's health drops to zero, they are incapacitated and left to fight off the Infected using a handgun until rescued by another Survivor. If a Survivor dies, they remain dead until the next level, unless revived by a defibrillator, or, in Campaign or Singleplayer mode, reappear in a "Rescue Closet" to be freed by other Survivors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Should all Survivors die or be incapacitated, the game will end, at which point the players may restart that chapter or quit the game.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_modes">Game modes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Game modes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> includes 5 regular game modes:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Campaign</b>: up to four human players fight against the Infected to make their way through Campaign stages; any Survivor not controlled by a human player is controlled by the computer.</li>
<li>A <b>Singleplayer</b> mode allows players to play without intrusion from human players, working through the Campaign stages with three computer-controlled Survivor allies.</li>
<li><b>Versus</b>: up to four other human players take control of various <a href="#The_Infected">Special Infected</a> to try and prevent the Survivors from completing a stage. Special Infected are randomly assigned to Infected players; they cannot control the Witch or any Common Infected. Occasionally, as determined by the AI Director, certain players will become the Tank. The two teams swap sides once per stage, and are scored based on their stage progress as Survivors. If both teams make it to the saferoom with all four Survivors, a 25-point tiebreaker is awarded to the team that dealt the most combined damage as Special Infected.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Survival_mode" title="Survival mode">Survival</a></b>: a timed challenge where the Survivors are trapped in a section of the campaign maps, and try to survive as long as possible against an unending onslaught of Infected.</li>
<li><b>Scavenge</b>: a new 4-on-4 mode that requires the Survivor players to collect and use as many fuel cans scattered about a level to fill up a power generator, while the Infected players attempt to stop them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> also features a <b>Realism</b> mode, which can be enabled at any difficulty for either Campaign or Versus. This mode removes some of the video-game aspects from the gameplay: Survivors cannot see each other's silhouettes, and dead teammates can only be revived with defibrillators and will not respawn later in the level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-realism_mode_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-realism_mode-15">[15]</a></sup> Weapons and other items will only glow when the player is within a few feet, forcing the players to search the levels more thoroughly. Headshots to enemies deal more damage, whereas limb or body shots require more shots.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In addition, the Witch enemy can kill any Survivor she would have normally incapacitated. Designed to force players to work closely together and rely on voice communication, Valve created Realism mode to give players a way "to be challenged as a team" without having to increase the difficulty level of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-realism_mode_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-realism_mode-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, in later versions of the game, there is a Mutation option, in which players can select from a menu of 30 variations, some singleplayer, some multiplayer (and some of the latter cooperative, some versus, or both). Each variation changes one or more major game dynamics, such as: constantly draining health, solo mode with no Survivor allies, death upon incapacitation, only one kind of weapon available, coop that later switches to versus, shooting or targeting constraints, an enemy type with increased power, increased numbers of Special Infected, etc. One of these modes, named GunBrain, is a weapons stats analyzer.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Infected">The Infected</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Infected">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While also referred to as zombies, the Infected are humans who have contracted a mutated strain of an infection, though neither the source nor nature of this "Green Flu" are made clear in the games. The most numerous Infected encountered by the survivors are the common Infected. Though individually weak, they can swarm and overwhelm the Survivors, especially when separated from their teammates. Damage to the infected in <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> is portrayed more realistically, with bullets and melee weapons ripping off bits of flesh and, in some cases, limbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> A new addition to <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> is the Uncommon Infected unique to each campaign. By virtue of location and equipment worn pre-infection, they possess abilities that separate them from the Common Infected. For example, the <i>Dead Center</i> campaign introduces infected CEDA agents in <a href="/wiki/Hazmat_suit" title="Hazmat suit">hazmat suits</a>, making them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fireproof" title="Fireproof">fireproof</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> <i>Dark Carnival</i> includes clowns, whose squeaking shoes attract small hordes of Common Infected;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <i>The Parish</i> includes infected <a href="/wiki/Private_security_company" title="Private security company">private security contractors</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riot-gear" title="Riot-gear">riot gear</a>, making them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulletproof" title="Bulletproof">bulletproof</a> from the front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>As in the first game, there are special Infected whose mutations grant them special abilities that make them highly dangerous, which act as <a href="/wiki/Boss_(video_gaming)" title="Boss (video gaming)">bosses</a>. The presence of such Infected nearby is hinted at by sound effects or musical cues unique to each type. The five Special Infected from the first game return in <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>, some with modified behavior and skin models:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Boomer</b>: an extremely bloated Infected who vomits bile. The bile attracts a horde of Common Infected on contact with Survivors and also momentarily blinds them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Upon death, it explodes and can also spray bile onto nearby Survivors.</li>
<li>The <b>Hunter</b>: an agile male Infected that can pounce on and incapacitate Survivors from great distances, tearing at them until the Survivor dies or another Survivor shoves it off/kills it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Smoker</b>: a male Infected with a long tongue that it uses to ensnare Survivors from a distance, continually choking them. Upon death, it releases a cloud of smoke that can obscure the Survivors' vision and cause them to cough, should they come in direct contact with the smoke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Tank</b>: a gigantic, extremely muscular Infected male with the strength to punch Survivors off their feet some distance, as well as toss cars and concrete slabs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Unless the Survivors work as a team, they will be quickly incapacitated or even killed by the Tank's inhuman strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Witch</b>: a crying Infected woman who, when provoked by either damage, loud sounds, light, or proximity of survivors, will attack the provoker and any other Survivors after her provoker is dead. She can incapacitate or even kill a Survivor in one hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Left_4_Dead.E2.80.94Infected_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Left_4_Dead.E2.80.94Infected-26">[26]</a></sup> <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> introduces a variant of the Witch that wanders aimlessly in the open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Left_4_Dead.E2.80.94Infected_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Left_4_Dead.E2.80.94Infected-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> also introduces three new Special Infected:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Charger</b>: a male Infected with an enormous right arm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and can charge into the Survivors, capturing and carrying one Survivor away from the others, sending any others in his path flying to the side after a capture and stunning survivors upon hitting an obstacle in a charge. He may then pummel his captured Survivor into the ground, rendering that Survivor helpless until one of their teammates helps them by killing the charger or stunning it with frag rounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Spitter</b>: a female Infected that spits out balls of stomach acid that splatter across an area, quickly eroding the Survivors' health as long as they remain within it. She also leaves a puddle of goo upon death. The longer a player loiters in the goo, the faster their health drops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Jockey</b>: a male Infected that jumps onto a Survivor's back and steers them into other Infected or environmental hazards (e.g. Spitter goo), whilst clawing at the player's head until the player is incapacitated, killed, or shoved off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku1-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku2_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku2-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OXM_50_Specials_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-OXM_50_Specials-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_AI_Director_2.0">The AI Director 2.0</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The AI Director 2.0">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As in the first game, an artificial intelligence system called the <a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead#AI_Director" title="Left 4 Dead">AI Director</a> drives gameplay by <a href="/wiki/Procedural_generation" title="Procedural generation">procedurally</a> spawning enemies, weapons and items based on players' performance during any given campaign. In <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>, the Director has been improved to encourage more participation by players, forcing players through difficult gauntlets to reach safety. It also has the ability to alter elements of the level, such as placement of walls, level layout, lighting, and weather conditions, making each play session unique.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup> The Director now rewards players for taking longer or more difficult paths through each episode by providing useful equipment, such as special ammo packs or higher tier weapons, along these riskier paths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e3preview_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-e3preview-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like its predecessor, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> is set in the aftermath of a worldwide pandemic of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">infectious disease</a> known as the "Green Flu", which rapidly transforms humans into zombie-like creatures and mutated forms that demonstrate extreme aggression towards non-infected (much like the infected in <i><a href="/wiki/28_Days_Later" title="28 Days Later">28 Days Later</a></i>). Few humans are immune to the disease, <a href="/wiki/Asymptomatic_carrier" title="Asymptomatic carrier">still carrying the infection but showing no symptoms</a>. The Civil Emergency and Defense Agency (CEDA) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">U.S. military</a> create safe zones to attempt to evacuate as many American survivors as possible. <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> introduces four new Survivors—Coach, Ellis, Nick, and Rochelle, who are immune to the disease and have individual back stories that are provided through character dialogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_producer_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_producer-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_coach_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_coach-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_gambler_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_gambler-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkc_01_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-darkc_01-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_mechanic_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_mechanic-41">[41]</a></sup> While the game is intended as a continuation of the original, occurring one week after the first game begins, Valve decided to create a new group of Survivors due to the change in location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joystiq_Lombardi_Interview_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joystiq_Lombardi_Interview-42">[42]</a></sup> Like the first game, the five campaigns in <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> are set across a story arc,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> set in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a>, which starts in <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a>, and ends in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans, Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e3preview_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-e3preview-4">[4]</a></sup> The four Survivors have to fight their way through hordes of Infected, using safehouses along the way to rest and recuperate in order to reach extraction points.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> features a new cast of human Survivors, which include: Coach (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Chad_Coleman" title="Chad Coleman">Chad Coleman</a>), a portly high-school football coach with a bad knee<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_coach_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_coach-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> (although it does not affect gameplay); Nick (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Dillon" title="Hugh Dillon">Hugh Dillon</a>), a cold and sarcastic gambler and con artist;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_gambler_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_gambler-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Rochelle (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Rochelle_Aytes" title="Rochelle Aytes">Rochelle Aytes</a>), a low-level production assistant reporting on the evacuation for a local television station;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_producer_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_producer-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> and Ellis (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Ladin" title="Eric Ladin">Eric Ladin</a>), a friendly (and rather talkative) mechanic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> who often talks about his friend Keith and their many misadventures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survivor_mechanic_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-survivor_mechanic-41">[41]</a></sup> In addition to the four playable characters, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> also features a <a href="/wiki/Non-player_character" title="Non-player character">supporting character</a> in the form of Virgil (voiced by Randall Newsome), a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cajun" title="Cajun">Cajun</a> boat captain, who appears (voice only) in the game's final three campaigns.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Story">Story</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Story">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Left_4_Dead_-_Dark_Carnival_screenshot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="125" data-file-width="250" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/Left_4_Dead_-_Dark_Carnival_screenshot.jpg/220px-Left_4_Dead_-_Dark_Carnival_screenshot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f1/Left_4_Dead_-_Dark_Carnival_screenshot.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Left_4_Dead_-_Dark_Carnival_screenshot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The amusement park in the campaign <b>Dark Carnival</b></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sacrifice_(Left_4_Dead)" title="The Sacrifice (Left 4 Dead)">The Sacrifice</a></b> DLC campaign takes place before the main events of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>; and after the events of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sacrifice_(Left_4_Dead)" title="The Sacrifice (Left 4 Dead)"><i>The Sacrifice</i> comic</a>. The original survivors of <i><a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead" title="Left 4 Dead">Left 4 Dead</a></i>—Bill, Francis, Louis, and Zoey—arrive at the portside town of Rayford, in order to search for a boat that can take them to the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> After finding an adequate sailboat, the Survivors have to manually start up generators in order to lift a bridge for their boat to pass through.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> One Survivor (canonically Bill) sacrifices himself in order to kick-start a generator once it gives out, so that the others may reach safety. This is the end of Bill's story in the <i>Left 4 Dead</i> video game series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> opens in <b>Dead Center</b> (set in <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a>), where the four Survivors find themselves abandoned on a hotel roof by rescue helicopters. They decide to head for the local mall, where a second CEDA evacuation point is located.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dc_01_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-dc_01-51">[51]</a></sup> After a brief encounter with a gun store owner, Whitaker (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Callie" title="Dayton Callie">Dayton Callie</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dc_02_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-dc_02-52">[52]</a></sup> the Survivors discover that the mall is overrun, with all CEDA agents having become either dead or infected as well. Ellis helps the group use a <a href="/wiki/Stock_car_racing" title="Stock car racing">stock car</a> to bust out of the mall<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dc_04_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-dc_04-7">[7]</a></sup> and travel towards New Orleans, rumored to be the last standing city in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dc_01.2_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-dc_01.2-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>The Passing</b> DLC campaign takes place between <i>Dead Center</i> and <i>Dark Carnival</i>, and after the events of <i>The Sacrifice</i> campaign. The Survivors of <i>L4D2</i> arrive at the bridge in Rayford, where they meet Francis, Louis, and Zoey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> As they need to cross the bridge to proceed, the Survivors need to find another way across to refill the generator with <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gas</a>. After fighting their way through a wedding reception (complete with a Witch bride),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> the streets, and a historic under-the-river tour,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> they meet up again with the original Survivors, who help by covering for the group while they fill the generator and lowering the bridge once it's full.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-passing_03_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-passing_03-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the start of the <b>Dark Carnival</b> campaign, the four Survivors find the highway ahead completely blocked by ditched vehicles, and are forced to travel on foot through an abandoned (but still-operating) amusement park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkc_01_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-darkc_01-40">[40]</a></sup> After navigating their way to the park stadium, Coach devises a plan to use a large-scale light show used by a rock band, The Midnight Riders, in order to signal a helicopter pilot for rescue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkc_05_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-darkc_05-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>After being rescued, they later discover that their pilot has been Infected. When the pilot starts attacking them, Nick is forced to kill him (echoing a similar situation in <i>Left 4 Dead</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>), causing the chopper to crash into a <a href="/wiki/Bayou" title="Bayou">bayou</a>, the setting for <b>Swamp Fever</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sf_01_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-sf_01-59">[59]</a></sup> Working their way through the swamps, the group comes across a crashed airplane, dead military paratroopers, and isolated swamp villages which had held out against the Infected but were eventually overrun. After spending the morning fighting through the swamp, the group arrives at a plantation mansion and make radio contact with Virgil, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cajun" title="Cajun">Cajun</a> boat captain who can assist them; however, his boat begins to run low on diesel fuel on the way to New Orleans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sf_05_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-sf_05-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_01_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-hr_01-61">[61]</a></sup> As a tumultuous rainstorm approaches (the titular <b>Hard Rain</b> of the subsequent campaign), the Survivors go ashore at Ducatel, Mississippi; make their way through an abandoned (and Witch-infested<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_02_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-hr_02-62">[62]</a></sup>) <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> mill to a gas station to get diesel fuel, and return to signal Virgil with an improvised "flare".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the final campaign, <b>The Parish</b>, Virgil drops the group off at New Orleans, where the military appears to be evacuating civilians across a bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_01_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-parish_01-64">[64]</a></sup> On the way there, the four discover the city overrun with Infected, and that the military is actually leaving the city before it is destroyed by an air strike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_02_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-parish_02-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_03_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-parish_03-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_04_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-parish_04-67">[67]</a></sup> The group manages to reach the bridge, where they make contact with the military. Judging from their dialogue, the military pilots suspect the Survivors to be "<a href="/wiki/Asymptomatic_carrier" title="Asymptomatic carrier">carriers</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_05_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-parish_05-68">[68]</a></sup> similar to the original Survivors of <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. After securing their rescue helicopter, the Survivors lower and cross the bridge, escaping on the helicopter just as the bridge is destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parish_05_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-parish_05-68">[68]</a></sup> While the Survivors' fate is left unclear after this point, Chet Faliszek, the game's writer, back in 2009 said that the military is taking survivors to cruise ships in the Caribbean in an attempt to escape the infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Development for <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> started shortly after the release of the first game—following a short break—building on ideas from the development team to make the next game "bigger and better".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_preview_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-rps_preview-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard-71">[71]</a></sup> The game was given the codename "Carnation" to prevent revealing its details before its official announcement;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstech_chet_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-arstech_chet-72">[72]</a></sup> Valve also considered a new title for the game, <i>Back 4 More</i>, though they eventually dropped it for <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Chet Faliszek stated that <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s story would explore more of the world of the game, and that Valve had created a full story for the cause and effects of the infection pandemic, including terms that they have used for the AI Director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstech_chet_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-arstech_chet-72">[72]</a></sup> Each campaign was purposely designed with a different feel; however, all five campaigns were mapped out at the same time by the entire team to provide the narrative flow and ensure the uniqueness of each campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxmuk_chet_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxmuk_chet-73">[73]</a></sup> The team used a <i>Left 4 Dead</i> dictionary developed to describe level design and flow within the game to provide a common language for developing the levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxmuk_chet_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-oxmuk_chet-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> contains about 7,800 unique lines of dialogue, a 40% increase over <i>Left 4 Dead</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l4d2_shading_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-l4d2_shading-74">[74]</a></sup> The writers designed the characters and selected appropriate voice actors who had natural accents for their lines and allowed the actors freedom to help authenticate the roles. They would attend recording sessions for the voice actors and allow them to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ad-lib" title="Ad-lib">ad-lib</a> their lines for their characters, often getting new ideas for character dialogue to be recorded later, particularly in the case of Ellis (voiced by Eric Ladin) and Nick (Hugh Dillon).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portal_2_writers_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-portal_2_writers-75">[75]</a></sup> Randall Newsome, the voice of the boat captain Virgil, was a local actor from Louisiana who naturally spoke <a href="/wiki/Cajun_French" title="Cajun French">Cajun</a> and helped to embellish the role better than the writers could.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portal_2_writers_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-portal_2_writers-75">[75]</a></sup> Faliszek wanted to include a "no-nonsense" woman from a <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Motor_Vehicles" title="Department of Motor Vehicles">Department of Motor Vehicles</a>, but this character did not make the cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstech_chet_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-arstech_chet-72">[72]</a></sup> The developers solicited several bands to include them in the game: <a href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode" title="Depeche Mode">Depeche Mode</a> responded eagerly, and allowed Valve to use its music and other imagery in the game, such as on Rochelle's T-shirt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In introducing the new Infected, the development team had to consider how the new abilities would mesh with the existing Infected and any changes they had made to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxmuk_chet_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-oxmuk_chet-73">[73]</a></sup> One discarded idea for a new Infected included the "Leaker"; the creature, when having taken damage, would shoot out spouts of goo at the survivors, and then would be able to self-detonate like the Boomer. However, this sacrificial act would have given survivors time to escape, and the idea was dropped, though features of the Leaker were built into the Spitter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxmuk_chet_73-3"><a href="#cite_note-oxmuk_chet-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In development, the programmers wanted to find a way to provide more variation and visual effects for the players, although they were already strained by memory limitations on the Xbox 360 for <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. One key development factor was recognizing a way to create greater variation in the appearance of the common infected through a number of modeling and rendering tasks. Simple changes of the underlying geometry of the model, either the head or the body, with the resulting effects on the texture mapping was one means to create apparent variation. Another means was created by using different head textures along with various blood and dirt maps, and similarly different wounds applied to the body texture. A final means to alter the tone of both the skin and the clothing worn by the infected. As a result, a single infected model could have up to 24,000 variations within the game. This allowed Valve to effectively only keep two to six common infected core models in memory for each level, leaving only the unique infected for each campaign and the special infected as their own unique models. As a result, the memory use for the infected dropped by 50%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l4d2_shading_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-l4d2_shading-74">[74]</a></sup> Valve's programmers also sought how to better represent damage the players did to the infected by showing inflicted wounds in the appropriate location and in a manner based on the weapon used, allowing for the inclusion of more resilient infected creatures in advanced game modes. They had simulated this in <i>Left 4 Dead</i> by having five possible character models that would result from a fatal attack but felt this could be advanced further. Already limited by memory concerns on the Xbox 360 that prevented further variations on the core infected models, the team devised a system of using textures with transparencies combined with ellipsoid culling from any infected character model to simulate the wounds, with several graphical process simplifications to avoid taxing the rendering system. This allowed the team to simulate up to two such wounds on each infected using only 13% of the memory resources of the based system in <i>Left 4 Dead</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another visual aspect that the Valve team explored was the rendering of water, particularly in the "Swamp Fever" campaign, which takes place mostly in a large swamp area. Valve found early play-testers would become confused with the large, tree-covered map, but by adding hints of water movement in the direction they were to go, there was a significant reduction in players becoming lost on the map. The water maps were created by using the 3D animation tool <a href="/wiki/Houdini_(software)" title="Houdini (software)">Houdini</a> against its landscape maps to create realistic water flow patterns as surface maps. These surface maps were then applied in a "flowing" manner instead of the scrolling manner used in previous games. These water effects were further expanded upon for Valve's next game, <i><a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">Portal 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Doug Lombardi, vice-president of marketing for Valve, noted that the <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">SDK</a> released for <i>Left 4 Dead</i> would also be compatible with <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-valve_protest_reply_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-valve_protest_reply-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>PC and Xbox 360 players who pre-ordered <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> through participating retailers gained early access to the game's demo, which was released on October 27, 2009 for Xbox Live and October 28, 2009 for PC players, and an exclusive baseball bat melee weapon to be used in game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Pre-ordering the PC version of the game through the Steam network also unlocks Bill's beret from <i>Left 4 Dead</i> for use in the PC version of <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Also, when a person buys the game and starts up Team Fortress 2, they will get a frying pan as a melee weapon and Ellis' hat as an in-game hat. The demo became available for all PC and Xbox Live Gold users on November 4, 2009 with Xbox Live Silver users gaining access on November 11, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The demo features the first two maps in "The Parish" campaign.</p>
<p>On October 5, 2009, Valve announced that <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> would be promoted by a $25 million advertising campaign, exceeding the $10 million that supported <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. The campaign includes television advertisements during sporting events, on billboards and magazines; and more aggressive advertising for Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valve_Corporation_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Valve_Corporation-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_updates">Release and updates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release and updates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> was released on Steam on November 17, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Retail copies were made available some days after, depending on the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2010, Valve announced that it would be bringing the Steam content platform to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X" title="Mac OS X">Mac OS X</a> computers; along with it, Steam will be providing native versions of existing Valve games including <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> and its <a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead" title="Left 4 Dead">predecessor</a>. The games will support cross-platform play, allowing Mac players to play alongside PC players on the same servers, and will also be part of its Steam Play cross-compatible and Steam Cloud titles, allowing a player who has purchased the game on one platform to download and play it on the other platform for free.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The Mac OS X client was released on October 5, 2010.</p>
<p>With the introduction of a Linux client for Steam, Valve has affirmed that <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> will be developed for Linux.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steam.E2.80.99d_Penguins_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steam.E2.80.99d_Penguins-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Linux version of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> was released on May 3, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Linux_Beta_Build_is_Live.21_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Linux_Beta_Build_is_Live.21-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 25, 2013, Valve released the game for free for new players. The Christmas update also included a special achievement called "Ghost of Christmas Present," awarded to veteran players who helped the free holiday players survive in the game's campaign mode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holiday_Gift_Giving_Time.21_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holiday_Gift_Giving_Time.21-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downloadable_content">Downloadable content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Downloadable content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="The_Passing"></span> On December 14, 2009, Valve announced the first <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">DLC</a> installment for <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>, "The Passing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-passingKotaku_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-passingKotaku-93">[93]</a></sup> Though initially planned to be released sometime in March 2010, "The Passing" was released on April 22, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The content costs 560 <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Points" title="Microsoft Points">Microsoft Points</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-passingKotaku_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-passingKotaku-93">[93]</a></sup> and is free for PC and Mac users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shacknews_passing_release_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_passing_release-95">[95]</a></sup> The campaign, taking place between the "Dead Center" and "Dark Carnival" campaigns, features the cast of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> meeting with three of the survivors from the original <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. The new group learns that the fourth original survivor, Bill, sacrificed himself to allow his comrades to continue on safely. The title "The Passing" can be interpreted in several ways; to Bill's passing, the brief passing encounter between the two groups, and of the first group of survivors "passing the torch" to the next.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gttv_passing_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-gttv_passing-96">[96]</a></sup> "The Passing" contains references to other zombie-themed works, including the games <i><a href="/wiki/Dead_Rising" title="Dead Rising">Dead Rising</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Plants_vs._Zombies" title="Plants vs. Zombies">Plants vs. Zombies</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and the movies <i><a href="/wiki/28_Days_Later" title="28 Days Later">28 Days Later</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Shaun_of_the_Dead" title="Shaun of the Dead">Shaun of the Dead</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_of_the_Dead_(1978_film)" title="Dawn of the Dead (1978 film)">Dawn of the Dead</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Dawn_of_the_Dead_(2004_film)" title="Dawn of the Dead (2004 film)">its remake</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>The add-on also features two new weapons, an <a href="/wiki/M60_machine_gun" title="M60 machine gun">M60 machine gun</a> which becomes unusable once depleted of ammo, and a golf club for melee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-passingKotaku_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-passingKotaku-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>A prequel to "The Passing", titled "The Sacrifice", was released on October 5, 2010, as an add-on for both <i>Left 4 Dead</i> and <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>. This prequel ties up the story of the original game, showing the events leading to the meeting of the two groups of survivors in "The Passing" from the point of the <i>Left 4 Dead</i> characters. However, players can choose which character will sacrifice themselves for the others to safely continue on and not just the canonical choice of Bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l4d2_sacrifice_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-l4d2_sacrifice-100">[100]</a></sup> Valve also provided the full "No Mercy" campaign from <i>Left 4 Dead</i> as a <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> campaign, which is playable with the original Survivors from <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. Though the maps are nearly identical to their appearance in <i>Left 4 Dead</i>, No Mercy in <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> contains all of the enhancements of the sequel, including the new Special Infected, Uncommon Infected, melee weapons, additional guns, and the ability to use the new game modes, including Mutations and Scavenge mode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l4d2_sacrifice_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-l4d2_sacrifice-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>An additional community-created downloadable content package, called "Cold Stream", was released July 24, 2012 for Xbox 360 and PC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Valve has announced testing had begun on the Xbox 360, as well as for all the original Left 4 Dead 1 maps via L4D Blog. The content is in public beta, available to players for testing and data collection on any issues, with a complete release date on 24 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> On July 24th it was announced that Valve did not send the downloadable content package to Microsoft. On August 1, 2012, it was announced that Cold Stream would be made available for Xbox 360 on August 3, at the price point of 560 MSP ($7).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>A proposed content package and <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie-in</a> for the 2012 horror film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cabin_in_the_Woods" title="The Cabin in the Woods">The Cabin in the Woods</a></i> was in the works, but the project dissolved after the film's original production company, <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">MGM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer#Attempted_sale_and_bankruptcy_protection" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">filed for bankruptcy</a>. The film's director, <a href="/wiki/Drew_Goddard" title="Drew Goddard">Drew Goddard</a>, commented on what the downloadable content would have included, stating: "The game was gonna be amazing. You were gonna be able to play in both the upstairs <i>Cabin in the Woods</i> world and the downstairs 'facility' world with all the monsters. Believe me, I HATE all video games based on movies, they always suck, but porting <i>Cabin</i> into <i>Left For Dead</i> felt like the right fit. It pains me that it didn't happen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 4, 2013 a <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_6" title="Resident Evil 6">Resident Evil 6</a></i> crossover DLC was released for the PC version. It adds the main characters and two monsters from <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> to the PC-exclusive The Mercenaries: No Mercy mode in <i>Resident Evil 6</i>. Also three monsters from <i>Resident Evil 6</i> are added as replacement skins to existing monsters on the PC version of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 20, 2015, an update for the game <i><a href="/wiki/Zombie_Army_Trilogy" title="Zombie Army Trilogy">Zombie Army Trilogy</a></i> was released, which imported the eight survivors from both <i>Left 4 Dead</i> games into <i>ZAT</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mutations">Mutations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mutations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mutations are modifications on <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s game modes, which have been offered every week after "The Passing"'s release; these game modes alter the conditions of play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shacknews_passing_release_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_passing_release-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrightHub_Passing_overview_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrightHub_Passing_overview-108">[108]</a></sup> All Mutations are now available through an update, making them selectable in the PC version. At this time Valve added the "Realism Versus" mutation to the game as a permanent game mode. All Mutations became available for Xbox 360 users with the release of Cold Stream.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_modification_support">Community modification support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Community modification support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Similar to <i>Left 4 Dead</i> and other Source Engine-based games, a number of players have constructed new maps, campaigns, and other variations for <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>, supported by Valve through their <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">software development kit</a> for the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> With the kit, players have found ways to include the original <i>Left 4 Dead</i> campaigns into <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Players have also found ways to increase the number of survivors up to 16, duplicating the graphics for the existing survivor characters as needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In August 2010, Valve announced that it will promote selected community generated maps, one every two weeks, both by blog posts on their official site, and by offering the map on a number of their dedicated servers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Valve updated the game in January 2013 to include support for Steam Workshop, allowing users to create and share new scenarios, maps, clothing and weapons. and to create Mutation-like changes that can be applied to existing maps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> A further patch in February 2013 introduced a new scripting system, Expanded Mutation System, that gives programmers more control and options to create new Mutations that can be played across any map or to customize behavior in specific campaigns; one such user-created Mutation creates an experience similar to the Zombie mode in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Black_Ops_2" title="Call of Duty: Black Ops 2">Call of Duty: Black Ops 2</a></i>, allowing players to buy weapons and barricades to fight off waves of zombies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_community_and_tournaments">Competitive community and tournaments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Competitive community and tournaments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On the PC, the original competitive modification named "Confogl", was created by community member ProdigySim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> It is now a playable mutation included in the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Confogl is a set of rules for competitive Left 4 Dead 2 versus which standardizes certain elements and changes the distribution of items and weapons. It tips the scales toward the infected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Tournaments have been held utilizing the Confogl modification, such as the CEVO tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
