<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> received critical acclaim from game journalists, praising the changes made with the new melee weapons and firearms, the new strategies introduced through the new special infected, and the details of the southern locale and individual campaigns compared with the campaigns of the first game. <a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a> praised the game's replayability and the attention put in every detail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L4D2review-ArsTechnica_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-L4D2review-ArsTechnica-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lib%C3%A9ration" title="Libération">Libération</a> also praised the game, commenting that Valve was one of the last game studios making games geared toward hardcore PC gamers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L4D2review-libe_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-L4D2review-libe-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> considered that the game improved on the first in every way, and that anyone who liked the concepts introduced by the first game should buy the second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign_review_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign_review-128">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurogamer" title="Eurogamer">Eurogamer</a> also praised the game, and considered that it was "overflowing with personality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eurogamer_review_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer_review-129">[129]</a></sup> <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> received the Best Xbox 360 Game award at the <a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">2009 Spike Video Game Awards</a>. The game has been nominated for the "Outstanding Achievement in Game Play Engineering", "Outstanding Achievement in Online Game Play", and "Action Game of the Year" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interactive_Achievement_Award" title="Interactive Achievement Award">Interactive Achievement Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Interactive_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_issues">Technical issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Technical issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Xbox 360 version of the game was noted at launch for having serious issues with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lag_(online_gaming)" title="Lag (online gaming)">lag</a> and slowdown in online game modes, the majority coming from using the game's dedicated servers. According to Valve, these problems were due to an unexpectedly huge number of players online on Xbox LIVE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-137">[137]</a></sup> It was shortly fixed after release by a server infrastructure change and adding new dedicated servers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Valve acknowledged problems with the PC version of the game upon launch, including inability to install the game, or users finding it crashed within minutes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Most users reported successful bug fixes from the patches that followed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Pre-release sales estimates for <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> were positive. As of July 2009, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> ranked first in purchase intent out of all upcoming games, with 9 out of 10 polled stating that they would buy the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> According to Lombardi, pre-orders for the sequel within the month following the announcement were double those for <i>Left 4 Dead</i> at the same time relative to release date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In a press release on October 5, 2009 Valve announced that, based on the strength of pre-orders, they expect <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> to be the fastest selling product in the company's history, with the game's pre-release sales averaging 300% greater than <i>Left 4 Dead</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valve_Corporation_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Valve_Corporation-84">[84]</a></sup> In an interview in November 2009, Chet Faliszek claimed the number of pre-sales of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> were four times that of the original game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4x_preorder_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-4x_preorder-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 1, 2009, Valve reported that more than two million retailed copies of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> were sold in two weeks, which represents "more than double" the sales of the original game's two week debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NPD_Group" title="NPD Group">NPD Group</a>, the Xbox 360 version was the fifth best-selling retail title for consoles in November 2009, with over 744,000 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2010, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> retail distributor, revealed that the game had sold 2.9 million on retail so far<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> wrote that more than 4 million copies were sold at stores in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over two weeks in July 2010, approximately 12,000 owners of <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Modern_Warfare_2" title="Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2">Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2</a></i> were mistakenly banned by <a href="/wiki/Valve_Anti-Cheat" title="Valve Anti-Cheat">Valve's-Anti-Cheat system</a>. Those affected received a free copy of the game or an extra copy to send as a gift.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_mw2bans_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-rps_mw2bans-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 10, 2011, Doug Lombardi mentioned that each of the <i>Left 4 Dead</i> games has sold 3 million copies on the Xbox 360.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> On August 11, 2011, in a phone interview with <a href="/wiki/Giant_Bomb" title="Giant Bomb">Giant Bomb</a>, Chet Faliszek said that the series had sold over 11 million units in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>For 24 hours on 25–26 December 2013, Valve offered <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> for free on PC using its Steam platform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> has been a central issue in a number of critical discussions regarding its timing and its graphic and mature content. <a href="/wiki/John_Walker_(journalist)" title="John Walker (journalist)">John Walker</a> of UK-based gaming website <a href="/wiki/Rock,_Paper,_Shotgun" title="Rock, Paper, Shotgun">Rock, Paper, Shotgun</a> has theorized that this is due to higher expectations for Valve, given the perception of its status as an industry leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps1_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-rps1-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boycott">Boycott</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Boycott">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The weekend following the game's announcement at the 2009 E3 Convention, some <i>Left 4 Dead</i> players called for a boycott of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> and formed the <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> community group called "L4D2 Boycott (NO-L4D2)" which grew to over 10,000 members by the end of that weekend,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up_boycott_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-1up_boycott-152">[152]</a></sup> and reached more than 37,000 about a month later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tvg_lombardi_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-tvg_lombardi-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> In addition to a lack of further <i>Left 4 Dead</i> content, they were concerned with the characters, visuals, and music shown in the E3 demonstration video, feeling these were inappropriate to the first game's aesthetics, and that the release of the sequel so soon after the first game would fracture the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up_boycott_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-1up_boycott-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to these complaints, Valve marketer Doug Lombardi stated that the announcement of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> at E3 should not be taken to indicate that Valve would no longer support the first game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tvg_lombardi_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-tvg_lombardi-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> He asked the community to "trust [them] a little bit," and told them that while their team was eager to get new material to players of <i>Left 4 Dead</i>, they determined that a sequel would be the best option for several reasons:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-valve_protest_reply_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-valve_protest_reply-79">[79]</a></sup> the demand for new campaigns, enemies and weapons could not be met as a simple DLC;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-valve_protest_reply_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-valve_protest_reply-79">[79]</a></sup> both Faliszek and project lead Tom Leonard found that too much of the content relied on each other, making it very difficult to release incremental patches in the same style as <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstech_chet_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-arstech_chet-72">[72]</a></sup> the development team liked the idea of rolling up the content into a sequel to be released a year after <i>Left 4 Dead</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra_l4d2_leonard-71">[71]</a></sup> Faliszek stated that Newell was skeptical of the idea when the team brought the sequel forward, but still allowed the project to go through.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstech_chet_72-4"><a href="#cite_note-arstech_chet-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009, Valve flew two of the boycott group's most prominent members to Valve, in order to playtest <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i>; the two felt that the sequel was well done.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> This event, through a series of correspondences made in jest, shortly led to Valve's <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Newell" title="Gabe Newell">Gabe Newell</a> and designer Erik Johnson flying to Australia to visit "Joe W-A", a <i>Left 4 Dead</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mod_(computer_gaming)" title="Mod (computer gaming)">modder</a>. Newell jokingly reported that Valve was "boycotting" Joe's new mod for the game when Joe asked when he would be flown to Valve in the same manner as the <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> boycotters, but whimsically offered that if Joe was to pay to fly him to the country, he would take a look at it. Joe was able to raise the required funds, US$3000, through donations through his website, though ultimately Newell paid for the trip himself, with Joe's collected donations going to the <a href="/wiki/Child%27s_Play_(charity)" title="Child's Play (charity)">Child's Play</a> charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 14, 2009, the initiators of the boycott group announced that they had ended their boycott and were shutting down the 40,000-plus group because Valve was retaining their promise of additional content and fixes for <i>Left 4 Dead</i>, such as the recent release of the "Crash Course" campaign. These gamers also believed that the group itself, losing its purpose, was now being used just to bad-mouth Valve and other players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> In a video interview posted on October 29, 2009, Gabe Newell said, "for people who joined the Boycott Group on Steam ... they're actually pre-ordering the product at a higher rate than Left 4 Dead 1 owners who weren't in the boycott".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_art">Cover art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cover art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Left_4_Dead_2_UK_cover.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="321" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Left_4_Dead_2_UK_cover.png/220px-Left_4_Dead_2_UK_cover.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/48/Left_4_Dead_2_UK_cover.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Left_4_Dead_2_UK_cover.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The UK version of the box art shows the back of the hand facing away to avoid offense</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Valve was forced to alter its original cover art for the game by the <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Software_Rating_Board" title="Entertainment Software Rating Board">ESRB</a>; the original image depicted the series' hand with its <a href="/wiki/Little_finger" title="Little finger">little finger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ring_finger" title="Ring finger">ring finger</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Thumb" title="Thumb">thumb</a> torn off, which would thus have the <a href="/wiki/Index_finger" title="Index finger">index finger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_finger" title="Middle finger">middle finger</a> remaining. It was deemed too explicit, but to appease the ESRB, Valve changed the image so that the fingers were merely bent back instead, but the company was still able to include the torn-off thumb in all regions except for Japan and Germany, where it had to be censored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coverart_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-coverart-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cover was further changed for release in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, as the two-finger sign with the back of the hand faced toward the viewer is considered an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V_sign_as_an_insult" title="V sign as an insult">insult</a>; the UK cover features the hand facing the opposite direction to avoid this, making it instead the more optimistic gesture for "Victory",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> even though it may not have been intended to be made insulting.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racism_accusations">Racism accusations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Racism accusations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Willie Jefferson of the <i><a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">Houston Chronicle</a></i>, after seeing initial promotional material for the game, considered that several of the infected "appear to be African-Americans" implying a <a href="/wiki/Race_and_video_games" title="Race and video games">racist</a> approach to the game, and also noted that "setting the game in a city that was a scene of dead, bloated bodies floating by" some years after the impact of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> was "a bad call".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Faliszek, commenting on Jefferson's claims, considered the supposition to be "utter insanity", and commented that the infected are a mix of all races, and that the game's version of New Orleans is "not a brick-for-brick representation" of the city and were not trying to make any statement about it with the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> A writer for <a href="/wiki/Kotaku" title="Kotaku">Kotaku</a> considered that Jefferson "seems to me to be picking a fight where none exists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Others noted that the appearance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> infected simply reflected the racial diversity of New Orleans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_ban_and_unbanning">Australian ban and unbanning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Australian ban and unbanning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_Film_and_Literature_Classification_(Australia)#Classification_of_video_games" title="Office of Film and Literature Classification (Australia)">Classification of video games by the Australian Office of Film and Literature Classification</a></div>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> was refused classification in Australia by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_Film_and_Literature_Classification_(Australia)" title="Office of Film and Literature Classification (Australia)">Office of Film and Literature Classification</a> (OFLC). It failed to gain a MA15+ rating, the highest possible rating for video games in Australia at the time of release. This prevented the sale of the original game within the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ban_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-ban-6">[6]</a></sup> In its report, the OFLC cited the reason for refusing classification as "realistic, frenetic and unrelenting violence".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> However, a small number of members of the OFLC board believed the game could merit the MA15+ rating which was used to publish the first <i>Left 4 Dead</i>. It was expected that changes could be made to the game to allow the game to be classified as MA15+ and thus sold in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Both Lombardi and Newell were "surprised" by the classification refusal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-au_remake_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-au_remake-172">[172]</a></sup> Valve appealed the OFLC's decision about a week after being notified of the ruling, comparing the sequel to its predecessor, which had been classified as MA15+, and the mature ratings the sequel had received from similar rating organizations around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> However, as the appeal process, expected to end on October 22, was close to the planned release date, Valve submitted a modified version of the game for classification addressing the concerns the OFLC has stated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-au_remake_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-au_remake-172">[172]</a></sup> This version, which no longer contained images of "decapitation, dismemberment, wound detail or piles of dead bodies", was classified as MA15+ by the OFLC, thus allowing for the game's release in Australia, though Valve and Electronic Arts still hoped to have their preferred, unmodified version classified by the OFLC for release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> The appeal of the decision to deny classification to the unedited version of the game was conducted by the independent Classification Review Board, and resulted in the previous ruling to deny classification being sustained. The Classification Review Board cited "insufficient delineation between the depiction of zombie characters and the human figures" as one of the key factors in its classification refusal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Left 4 Dead 2</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s classification refusal, as well as for other recent games such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fallout_3" title="Fallout 3">Fallout 3</a></i> (has since been rerated MA15+ having the same version as other countries) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aliens_vs._Predator_(video_game)" title="Aliens vs. Predator (video game)">Aliens vs. Predator</a></i> (has since appealed and rerated MA15+ uncut), has reignited debate over the current prohibition of sale and exhibition of video games for mature audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> In mid-December 2009, the Australian government sought public opinion on the adult classification rating for video games, despite statements by South Australian Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Michael_Atkinson" title="Michael Atkinson">Michael Atkinson</a> believing the issue to only affect a minority of the country's citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Following Atkinson's decision to leave the Attorneys General to be replaced by <a href="/wiki/John_Rau" title="John Rau">John Rau</a>, who is reportedly in favour of an R18+ rating,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Valve have revealed that, should the bill be passed, they plan to release an uncensored version of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> for PC in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Australian Federal Parliament has passed R18+ classification for video games which came into effect on January 1, 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and Valve is exploring legal options of resubmitting an R18+ version of <i>Left 4 Dead 2</i> following this change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 29, 2014, the uncensored version was reclassified R18+, effectively unbanning the game, five years after the original release, with Valve adding in the availability to switch to the uncensored version as <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">DLC</a> for all users running who purchased L4D2 in Australia before it was reclassified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_ban">German ban</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Left_4_Dead_2&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: German ban">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_banned_video_games#Germany" title="List of banned video games">List of banned video games § Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Germany" title="Video gaming in Germany">Video gaming in Germany</a></div>
<p>In order to achieve the highest possible rating given by <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Unterhaltungssoftware_Selbstkontrolle" title="Unterhaltungssoftware Selbstkontrolle">Unterhaltungssoftware Selbstkontrolle</a> (<i>Freigegeben ab 18 Jahren gemäß § 14 JuSchG</i>, meaning "Restricted for those below the age of 18"), Valve had to heavily censor the game's violent content similar to the Australian version. However, the international (and thus uncensored) version was <a href="/wiki/Federal_Department_for_Media_Harmful_to_Young_Persons#The_indexing_process" title="Federal Department for Media Harmful to Young Persons">indexed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Department_for_Media_Harmful_to_Young_Persons" title="Federal Department for Media Harmful to Young Persons">Federal Department for Media Harmful to Young Persons</a> on December 1, 2009 in order to prevent sellers from advertising or selling it to minors. On February 15, 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Amtsgericht" title="Amtsgericht">Amtsgericht</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten,_Berlin" title="Tiergarten, Berlin">Tiergarten</a> confiscated all European PC versions for violation of <a href="/wiki/Strafgesetzbuch#.C2.A7_131:_Representation_of_violence" title="Strafgesetzbuch">§ 131 StGB</a> (representation of violence), meaning they may not be sold; however, it is still legal to import (with the risk that the game is confiscated by customs) and own the game. The court said that the game trivializes violence due to its high killing rate and explicit graphical representation of mutilation. They also sensed a strong cynical attitude behind the game's concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> To make up for the censorship, German players receive exclusive weapons ported from <i><a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Source" title="Counter-Strike: Source">Counter-Strike: Source</a></i>, which include the <a href="/wiki/Heckler_%26_Koch_MP5" title="Heckler &amp; Koch MP5">Heckler &amp; Koch MP5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accuracy_International_AWM" title="Accuracy International AWM">Accuracy International AWM</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SIG_552" title="SIG 552">SIG 552</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steyr_Scout" title="Steyr Scout">Steyr Scout</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Combat_knife" title="Combat knife">combat knife</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
